In [187]:
#creating and writing table data into a csv file
with open('priceday.csv', 'w') as f:
    writer = csv.writer(f)
    for table in page_data.find_all("tbody"):
        for trs in table.find_all('tr'):
            tds = trs.find_all('td')
            row = [elem.text.strip() for elem in tds]
            print(row)
            writer.writerow(row)

In [200]:
# Create a line chart to roughly see the price trend 
# From the plot, it is obvious that there are three stages. 
#One is from around 100 rising to 1000 during 2013
#The second is when the the price dropped again below 1000 then rised again to 1000 between Jan 2014 to Jan 2017
#The third is a rapid increasing period from 1000 to more than 10000 just during 2017
trace0 = go.Scatter(
    x = pricedaily.index,
    y = pricedaily.Open,
    mode = 'lines',
    name = 'Open'
)
trace1 = go.Scatter(
    x = pricedaily.index,
    y = pricedaily.High,
    mode = 'lines',
    name = 'High'
)
trace2 = go.Scatter(
    x = pricedaily.index,
    y = pricedaily.Close,
    mode = 'lines',
    name = 'Close'
)
data = [trace0, trace1, trace2]
layout = dict(title = 'Daily Bitcoin Price(Open, High and Close)From 2013-2017',
              xaxis = dict(title = 'Day'),
              yaxis = dict(title = 'USD'),
              )
fig = dict(data=data, layout=layout)
py.iplot(fig, filename='line-mode')

High five! You successfully sent some data to your account on plotly. View your plot in your browser at https://plot.ly/~ryzzz1121/0 or inside your plot.ly account where it is named 'line-mode'

)
trace1 = go.Bar(

    y = pricedaily.Volume,
    name = "Volume"
)

    x = pricedaily.index,
    y = pricedaily["Market Capitalization"],
    mode = 'makers',
    name = 'Market Capitalization'
)
data = [trace0, trace1, trace2]
layout = dict(title = 'Daily Bitcoin Close Price, Volume, Market Capitalization From 2013-2017',
              )
fig = dict(data=data, layout=layout)
py.iplot(fig, filename='bar-line')

#creating a function to check the data when the price was between certain amount 
def check_price_table(minValue,MaxValue):
    price=pricedaily[(pricedaily["Close"].values >=int(minValue))&(pricedaily["Close"].values <=int(MaxValue))]
    return price

In [207]:
#creating a function to check whether after the price reached certain value it droped again and such situation happened in how many days
def check_price_drop_days(minValue,MaxValue):
    price=pricedaily[(pricedaily["Close"].values >=int(minValue))&(pricedaily["Close"].values <=int(MaxValue))]
    #print(price)
    priced=pricedaily[(pricedaily.index >= price.index[0])&(pricedaily.index <= price.index[-1])] 
    different_days=priced.shape[0]-price.shape[0]
    print( "After the bitcoin price reached {}, it droped again. And such situation happened \nfor {} days before the price got stable above {}." .format(minValue,different_days,minValue))
    for i in priced.index:
        if i not in price.index:
                print(i)
                
    

check_price_drop_days(1000,2000)

After the bitcoin price reached 1000, it droped again. And such situation happened 
for 1215 days before the price got stable above 1000.

In [209]:
#creating a function to count the days bitcoin took to first reach certain value(including the day it reached that value)
def count_days(low_price,high_price):
    priceday1=pricedaily[(pricedaily["Close"].values >=int(low_price))]
    priceday2=pricedaily[(pricedaily["Close"].values >=int(high_price))]
    print(priceday2.index[0]-priceday1.index[0])

count_days(0, 1000)    

213 days 00:00:00

#line chart of 2017 bitcoin price,gold price, curde oil price cpmparison

    x = pricedaily2017.index,
    y = pricedaily2017.Close,
    mode = 'lines',
    name = 'bitcoin price'
)

trace1 = go.Scatter(
    x = goldprice2017.Date,
    y = goldprice2017["USD (PM)"],
    mode = 'lines',
    name = 'gold price'
)

trace2 = go.Scatter(
    x = oilprice2017.DATE,
    y = oilprice2017["DCOILWTICO"],
    mode = 'lines',
    name = 'Crude oil price'
)

data = [trace0,trace1,trace2]
layout = dict(title = 'Daily Bitcoin Price, Gold Price, Crude Oil Price in 2017')


fig = dict(data=data, layout=layout)

#subset a monthly bitcoin price dataset to calculate monthly price change
datelist=["2017-01-15","2017-02-15","2017-03-15","2017-04-15",
          "2017-03-15","2017-04-15","2017-05-15","2017-06-15",
          "2017-07-15","2017-08-15","2017-09-15","2017-10-15",

In [229]:
#calculate the change rate in percent 
#first row can't be calculated using zero instead
changelist=[0,]
for i in range(1,pmonthly.shape[0]):
            change=pmonthly.Close[i]-pmonthly.Close[i-1]
            change_rate=change/pmonthly.Close[i-1]
            #print(change_rate)
            pct=round(change_rate*100,2)
            changelist.append(pct)
            #print(changelist)


pmonthly=pmonthly.assign(Change  = changelist)

#the largest change rate happened between 2013-10 and 2013-11 which is 187.77%
pmonthly.Change.sort_values()
Out[229]:

with open('othercoinprice.csv', 'w') as m:
    writer = csv.writer(m)
    for table in crypage_data.find_all("tbody"):
        for trs in table.find_all('tr'):
            tds = trs.find_all('td')
            row = [elem.text.strip() for elem in tds]
            print(row)
            writer.writerow(row)

In [247]:
#line chart for all housing price over the years 
trace0 = go.Scatter(
    x = housing_price.DATE,
    y = housing_price["USSTHPI"],
    mode = 'lines',
    name = 'housing price'
)


data = [trace0]
layout = dict(title = 'Daily Housing Price index during 1975 to 2015'
              )


fig = dict(data=data, layout=layout)
py.iplot(fig, filename='line-model')

trace0 = go.Scatter(
    x = np.arange(331),
    y = pricedaily2017.Close,
    mode = 'lines',
    name = 'bitcoin price'
)
trace1 = go.Scatter(
    x = np.arange(331),
    y = nas_pricerising["NASDAQCOM"],
    mode = 'lines',
    name="NASDAQ Composite Index"
    
)
